# Experiment Plan and Results Analysis

## Experiment Plan Overview

The experiment aims to test the hypothesis that "Advanced preprocessing techniques like CLAHE enhancement and vessel extraction will significantly improve model performance on noisy fundus images compared to basic normalization."

**Control Group:**
- Preprocessing: Basic normalization
- Model: EfficientNetB4

**Experimental Group (planned but not executed):**
- CLAHE enhancement + EfficientNetB4
- Gaussian blur + EfficientNetB4
- Ben Graham preprocessing + EfficientNetB4
- Vessel extraction + EfficientNetB4

## Execution Status
- Control group experiment has been completed
- Experimental group tests have not been executed yet

## Control Group Results

The control group experiment using basic normalization and EfficientNetB4 was successfully completed with these results:

- **Training duration:** 116m 32s (1 hour 56 minutes)
- **Best validation metrics (at epoch 9):**
  - Quadratic Weighted Kappa: 0.8984
  - Accuracy: 0.8316
- **Final training metrics (at epoch 10):**
  - Loss: 0.3520
  - Kappa: 0.9202
  - Accuracy: 0.8695
- **Final validation metrics (at epoch 10):**
  - Loss: 0.5926
  - Kappa: 0.8931
  - Accuracy: 0.8361

The model was trained with:
- Batch size: 4
- Epochs: 10
- Early stopping patience: 5
- Dataset split: 2636 training images, 659 validation images, 367 test images

The experimental setup encountered some initial technical issues (as seen in the earlier runs without metrics), but the final run completed successfully with the metrics reported above.
# Experiment Plan and Raw Results

Based on the provided information, here is the experiment plan and the raw results:

## Experiment Plan
- **Hypothesis**: Domain-specific data augmentation techniques tailored for retinal images will improve model generalization and performance on the private test set compared to generic augmentations.
- **Dataset**: APTOS 2019 Kaggle dataset (train.csv for training; test.csv for testing)
- **Task**: Detect diabetic retinopathy from retina images, predicting severity on a 0-4 scale

### Controlled Variables
- Model architecture: EfficientNetB4
- Preprocessing: CLAHE enhancement
- Dataset: APTOS 2019
- Training hyperparameters

### Independent Variables
- Data augmentation strategies:
  - Minimal augmentation (Control Group): only horizontal/vertical flips and small rotations
  - Extensive augmentation: adds zoom, shift, brightness variations
  - Class-balanced augmentation: oversamples minority classes
  - Domain-specific augmentation: retina-specific transformations like varying lighting conditions and simulated noise

### Dependent Variables
- Quadratic weighted kappa score
- Accuracy
- Model generalization ability

## Raw Results

The experiment has been partially executed, with only the control group (minimal augmentation) being completed.

### Control Group Results (Minimal Augmentation)
- **Model**: EfficientNetB4
- **Preprocessing**: CLAHE enhancement
- **Augmentation**: Minimal (horizontal/vertical flips, small rotations)
- **Class balancing**: Weighted loss function

#### Dataset Information
- Train images count: 3,295
- Test images count: 367
- Class distribution:
  - Class 0: 1,628 (49.41%)
  - Class 1: 340 (10.32%)
  - Class 2: 896 (27.19%)
  - Class 3: 176 (5.34%)
  - Class 4: 255 (7.74%)

#### Training Results
- **Epoch 1**: Train Loss: 1.2013, Train Acc: 63.92%, Val Loss: 1.0595, Val Acc: 74.96%, Val Kappa: 0.8016
- **Epoch 2**: Train Loss: 0.8120, Train Acc: 77.85%, Val Loss: 0.8785, Val Acc: 76.02%, Val Kappa: 0.8570

#### Final Validation Metrics
- **Accuracy**: 0.7602
- **Quadratic Weighted Kappa**: 0.8570

### Experimental Group
The experimental group with extensive, class-balanced, and domain-specific augmentation strategies has not been completed yet according to the provided information.
# Experiment Results: APTOS 2019 Diabetic Retinopathy Detection

## Experiment Setup
- **Dataset**: APTOS 2019 Kaggle dataset (3,295 training images, 367 test images)
- **Task**: Classify diabetic retinopathy severity (5 classes, 0-4 scale)
- **Class Distribution**: Class 0: 1,628, Class 1: 340, Class 2: 896, Class 3: 176, Class 4: 255
- **Model Architecture**: EfficientNet-B4 with pretrained weights
- **Validation Strategy**: 5-fold cross-validation
- **Metrics**: Cohen's Kappa score, Accuracy

## Control Group Results (Single Model Approach)
Only partial results were obtained due to memory constraints:

| Fold | Best Validation Kappa | Accuracy | Status |
|------|------------------------|----------|--------|
| 1    | 0.9236                | 0.8589   | Completed |
| 2    | 0.9259                | 0.8483   | Completed |
| 3    | N/A                   | N/A      | Failed (memory error) |
| 4    | N/A                   | N/A      | Failed during 2nd epoch |
| 5    | 0.8326                | 0.7466   | Partially completed (1 epoch) |

## Experimental Group
The experimental group testing (ensemble methods) was not completed due to the technical challenges encountered in the control group.

## Technical Issues
- Multiple "Bus error" crashes related to insufficient shared memory
- DataLoader workers exited unexpectedly during training
- Memory constraints prevented completion of the full 5-fold cross-validation
- Model loading failed for some folds during prediction attempts
- Final evaluation encountered an "attempt to get argmax of an empty sequence" error

## Preliminary Conclusions
The control group showed promising initial performance with Kappa scores above 0.92 for completed folds, but the experiment requires system optimization to complete all planned evaluations and properly test the ensemble methods against the single model approach.
# Raw Experimental Results for Diabetic Retinopathy Detection

## Dataset Information
- Source: APTOS 2019 Kaggle dataset
- Split: 2,636 training images, 659 validation images, 367 test images
- Task: Detection of diabetic retinopathy severity (5-class classification, scale 0-4)

## Training Configuration
- Model architecture: EfficientNetB4 (pretrained)
- Input size: Standard EfficientNetB4 input dimensions
- Hardware: NVIDIA A40 GPU with CUDA
- Training approach: Control group using standard regularization, end-to-end training
- Duration: 10 epochs (~424 seconds per epoch, ~74 minutes total)

## Per-Class Performance (Based on Best Model - Epoch 3)
- Class 0 (No DR): 99.39% accuracy
- Class 1 (Mild): 29.03% accuracy
- Class 2 (Moderate): 86.26% accuracy
- Class 3 (Severe): 75.76% accuracy
- Class 4 (Proliferative): 30.19% accuracy

## Performance Pattern
- Training loss consistently decreased throughout all epochs (from 0.7234 to 0.1309)
- Validation performance peaked at Epoch 3
- Clear signs of overfitting after Epoch 3 (training loss continued to decrease while validation metrics deteriorated)
- Strong class imbalance evidenced by poor performance on classes 1 (Mild) and 4 (Proliferative)

## Total Execution Time
- Approximately 4,417 seconds (73.6 minutes)

Based on the provided information, I can see the experimental plan and partial results from the control group experiment.

## Experiment Plan Overview
- **Hypothesis**: Extended training with appropriate learning rate schedules will significantly improve model performance beyond what was achieved in the 2-epoch baseline, especially with proper regularization to prevent overfitting.

- **Control Group**: 
  - EfficientNetB4 model with CLAHE enhancement preprocessing
  - Best augmentation from previous experiment
  - 2 epochs
  - Constant learning rate

- **Experimental Group** (planned but not yet executed):
  - Configuration 1: 10 epochs, constant learning rate
  - Configuration 2: 20 epochs, cosine annealing learning rate schedule
  - Configuration 3: 30 epochs, one cycle learning rate schedule

## Control Group Results
The control experiment used EfficientNetB4 with CLAHE enhancement preprocessing, trained for 2 epochs with constant learning rate of 0.0001. The experiment was conducted on the APTOS 2019 dataset which includes:
- Train samples: 3296
- Test samples: 368

The training was run on an NVIDIA A40 GPU with PyTorch 2.7.0.

From the logs, we can see the first epoch was completed, showing:
- Epoch 1 - Train Loss: 0.8204
- Validation Loss: 0.6348
- Validation Quadratic Weighted Kappa: 0.8386
- Validation Accuracy: 0.7800

The logs show that the model was saved as the best model after the first epoch. However, the logs provided don't show the complete results for the second epoch or the final model performance on the test set.

The experimental group configurations with extended training (10, 20, and 30 epochs) and different learning rate schedules have not been executed yet according to the plan status.
# Experiment Plan and Raw Results

## Experiment Plan
The experiment is focused on developing a machine learning model to detect diabetic retinopathy from retina images with severity classified on a 0-4 scale. The experiment tests different class balancing techniques to address imbalance in the APTOS 2019 Kaggle dataset.

**Hypothesis:** Advanced class balancing techniques will significantly improve per-class accuracy for underrepresented classes (particularly Class 1 and Class 4) while maintaining high overall quadratic weighted kappa scores.

**Control Group:**
- Model: EfficientNetB4
- Class balancing: weighted_loss
- Preprocessing: CLAHE_enhancement

**Experimental Group:**
- All use EfficientNetB4 with CLAHE_enhancement, but with different class balancing techniques:
  - focal_loss
  - oversampling
  - class_balanced_sampling
  - two_stage_training

## Raw Results

### Control Group Results (weighted_loss):

**First Run:**
- Test Accuracy: 0.7818
- Test Quadratic Weighted Kappa: 0.8721
- Per-Class Accuracy:
  - Class 0: 0.9915
  - Class 1: 0.2549
  - Class 2: 0.7687
  - Class 3: 0.1786
  - Class 4: 0.6857

**Second Run:**
- Test Accuracy: 0.8242
- Test Quadratic Weighted Kappa: 0.8970
- Per-Class Accuracy:
  - Class 0: 0.9915
  - Class 1: 0.6078
  - Class 2: 0.7959
  - Class 3: 0.4286
  - Class 4: 0.4571

The training was conducted for 10 epochs with early stopping in the first run (stopped after 6 epochs). The model used pretrained weights for EfficientNet-B4 and was evaluated on the test set.

The experimental group results were not included in the provided raw data.
# Experimental Results Summary

Based on the provided experimental plan and raw results, here is a summary of the diabetic retinopathy detection experiment:

## Experiment Setup
- **Model**: EfficientNetB4
- **Preprocessing**: CLAHE enhancement
- **Training Configuration**: Best configuration from previous experiments
- **Dataset Distribution**: 
  - Total training samples: 3,295
  - Class distribution in training:
    - Class 0 (No DR): 1,628 samples
    - Class 1 (Mild): 340 samples
    - Class 2 (Moderate): 896 samples
    - Class 3 (Severe): 176 samples
    - Class 4 (Proliferative DR): 255 samples
  - Test samples: 367

## Training Results
- **Training/Validation Split**: 2,636 training samples, 659 validation samples
- **Best Performance**: Achieved at epoch 8
- **Training Duration**: 113 minutes 13 seconds
- **Early Stopping**: Applied at epoch 18

## Performance Metrics on APTOS Test Dataset
- **Validation Quadratic Weighted Kappa**: 0.9096
- **Validation Accuracy**: 0.8376
- **Per-class Accuracy**:
  - Class 0: 98.78%
  - Class 1: 66.15%
  - Class 2: 76.88%
  - Class 3: 46.88%
  - Class 4: 56.25%

## Observations
- The model shows very good overall performance on the APTOS test dataset
- Class 0 (No DR) has excellent detection accuracy
- Lower classes (mild, moderate) perform reasonably well
- Severe and proliferative DR (classes 3 and 4) have lower accuracy, likely due to class imbalance in the training data

Note: According to the experimental plan, this represents only the control group results on the APTOS test dataset. The experimental group results testing on EyePACS, APTOS with synthetic noise, and Messidor-2 datasets were not included in the provided output.
